                     <div class="attribution-component D-b W-100" id="article-aft-attribution-toyota-road-concept-revives-three-wheel-microcar-162115110" style="max-width:305px;">

                        <div class="pre-cut" style="height:auto;margin-bottom:1.5em;">
                         <p>
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:9a4d336c-96e5-3955-b02e-b823a8d13691;t9:18;itc:0" href="https://s.yimg.com/oy/photos/toyota-i-road-concept-vehicle-slideshow/" target="_blank">
                           <img alt="Toyota i-ROAD concept revives the three-wheel microcar" class="aligncenter size-large wp-image-10448 editorial" height="386" src="https://s.yimg.com/lo/api/res/1.2/yAG.fSOa_JBEoKULPPI2ow--/YXBwaWQ9bWFnYXppbmVzO3c9ODAw/https://s.yimg.com/os/en-US/blogs/motoramic/toyotairoadtop.jpg" width="800"/>
                          </a>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          In Terry Gilliam's classic movie "Brazil," Sam Lowry drives around a dystopian future cityscape in a three-wheel Messerschmitt KR200, a 1950s-era European microcar that looks equal parts cool and ridiculous. For this year's Geneva Motor Show,
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:9a4d336c-96e5-3955-b02e-b823a8d13691;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://autos.yahoo.com/toyota" target="_blank">
                           Toyota
                          </a>
                          has taken the idea of a three-wheel, tandem-seat microcar to a modern extreme in a concept it calls i-ROAD, and because the future has more in common with "Brazil" than we might prefer.
                          <span id="more-10447">
                          </span>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Most major automakers are working on ideas of vehicles that fill the space between a small car and a motorcycle  something small enough to fit in tight urban environments, but sizable enough to provide weather and crash protection so that passengers wouldn't have to wear helmets. None has advanced to the point of production, and the slow progress of a few start-ups has made such vehicles seem an answer to a question not many people have thought to ask yet.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          But the trend lines say rising fuel prices and crowded metropolises will eventually demand a replacement for the four-wheel compact car. In the i-ROAD, Toyota combines an electric motor and battery that can travel 30 miles on a charge with a stability system to keep the trike upright; its front wheels raise and lower in turns to lean the body without toppling it. By seating two people in tandem, Toyota says the i-ROAD is no wider than a conventional motorcycle, and would require no special training to drive.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:9a4d336c-96e5-3955-b02e-b823a8d13691;t9:18;itc:0" href="https://s.yimg.com/oy/photos/toyota-i-road-concept-vehicle-slideshow/" target="_blank">
                           <img alt="" class="aligncenter size-large wp-image-10450 editorial" data-src="https://s.yimg.com/lo/api/res/1.2/3JAtHV7crzVzqxHJ3CCBxw--/YXBwaWQ9bWFnYXppbmVzO3c9ODAw/https://s.yimg.com/os/en-US/blogs/motoramic/toyotairoadcombo-copy.jpg" height="407" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" width="800"/>
                          </a>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          The chances of Toyota building a 21st-century Messerschmitt hover close to zero at the moment; the world's largest automaker has plenty of demand for its real vehicles, and as the
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:9a4d336c-96e5-3955-b02e-b823a8d13691;t9:18;itc:0" href="https://s.yimg.com/oy/scion/iQ" target="_blank">
                           Scion iQ
                          </a>
                          shows, four-wheel cars can get far smaller than most people find comfortable. But it's impossible to rule that such vehicles will never emerge, and there may yet be a formula for drivers who want to lean into the future.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <iframe data-src="https://www.youtube.com/embed/ScsDvRYyitc?list=PLMJ_oV58WE4Ef1huEr4ILQv5FvueGhjN6" frameborder="0" height="354" width="630">
                          </iframe>
                         </p>
                        </div>
                        <div class="post-cut W-100" id="post-cut" style="transition-property:none;-webkit-transition-property:none;transition-duration:10s;-webkit-transition-duration:10s;transition-timing-function:ease-in;-webkit-transition-timing-function:ease-in;overflow:hidden;max-height:999999px;max-width:500px;">
                        </div>
                       </div>
                      </div>

                     <div class="item Td-n Pos-r D-b Ov-h SlowTrans has-image" id="article-aft-image-link-toyota-road-concept-revives-three-wheel-microcar-162115110-124084405802" style="padding:0 0 40px;">

Then, Volvo quickly sold out of a very small production run of 2015 S60\u002FV70 Polestars&#x2014;only 40 sedans and 80 wagons were built that year; our test car was #73. With full ownership of Polestar, Volvo says that Polestar models will increase to 1,000&#x2013;1,500 globally in the medium term, about double the number of units Polestar built for Volvo for 2016, yet still qualifying as rare and special things.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EWhile current Polestars are motivated by Volvo&#x2019;s turbocharged inline-6, Volvo said that future Polestars will utilize Volvo&#x2019;s innovative twin-engine electrification (ie: plug-in hybrid) technology to achieve their performance targets. So, not only will they be quicker, but they will be greener, too. And alas, way more expensive, too.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EVolvo will also sell Polestar performance-optimizing kits for existing models. the Costly Reality of Run-Flat Tires","summary":"Ready to tackle this misfortune, he looked for a spare tire in the trunk, but there was none to be found.  Without the option to solve the dilemma on his own, he called BMW roadside assistance, only to be told there was no spare tire since the car comes with run-flats.","body":"\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w900\u002F1a7c120c1180539356f36886dd992bc0a13bb240.jpg\" alt=\"Deflating the Costly Reality of Run-Flat Tires\" width=\"900\" height=\"647\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003ERun-flat tires promise to remove a key travel worry&#x2014;being stranded roadside. However, the ownership experience can be both expensive and frustrating, as we have heard from owners.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EA reader recently recounted a nightmarish run-flat tire tale that captures the potential downsides to this technology and mirrors other feedback we have received. (Even our staff has had their own run-flat adventures.)\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThis consumer wrote us about driving his dream car, a \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fautos\u002Fresearch\u002Fbmw\u002F5-series\u002F2016\u002F4dr-sdn-550i-rwd\"\u003E2012 BMW 550i\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, on a long trip. When a tire-pressure warning light illuminated, he pulled off the highway, stopped, and discovered a flat tire. Ready to tackle this misfortune, he looked for a spare tire in the trunk, but there was none to be found.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EWithout the option to solve the dilemma on his own, he called \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fautos\u002Fresearch\u002Fbmw\u002F\"\u003EBMW\u003C\u002Fa\u003E roadside assistance, only to be told there was no spare tire since the car comes with run-flats.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EBecause the flat was caused by a sidewall failure, the owner was told not to drive on it.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003ELate on a Sunday night, far from home, the driver spent 2 &#xBD; hours waiting for a flat-bed tow to get the expensive car to safe ground, followed by an unexpected night in a hotel. &#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThe disappointed owner got his car back on the road the next day and was fairly satisfied knowing flats are a rare event. But he felt that he would have bought a different car with regular tires instead of the run-flats, had he known.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003ESince the initial troublesome experience, the owner was stranded four more times, accumulating a total of eight road-hazard flats in less than 30,000 miles. Adding insult to injury, in the best of times, the owner found the run-flats to be stiff riding and noisy. Plus, they cost a bundle to replace (claimed $500 apiece) and even at that, replacements are hard to find.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" width=\"700\" height=\"374\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w700\u002F37b3c783643327ce7f252c550d7f3155b2f00501.jpg\"\u003E \n\u003Ci\u003ERun-flat tires are standard with many luxury vehicles like the BMW 5 Series, pictured here.\u003C\u002Fi\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EAlthough eight failures is extreme for any car, the issues related to comfort and replacement are not unique to this individual. We&#x2019;ve heard them similar complaints from many others. In this case, a BMW dealer suggested he buy tire insurance for a mere $2,500&#x2014;an astronomical sum that sounded ridiculous at the time. To be fair, the owner confided a BMW dealer did make some concessions on the cost of some of the replacement tires, but he no longer has confidence in his beloved car.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThe owner suggests that anyone buying a car with run-flats inquire about tire insurance and negotiate the price down to make the car deal happen. We estimate that about 15 percent of the cars sold last year came with run-flats, so be sure to ask the dealer what kind of tires are on the car before you buy it. Many cars today come with just a tire repair kit, rather than a spare tire. Be sure you are getting what you expect when you buy a car, and if it doesn&#x2019;t include a spare, ask if one is available.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EHave you experienced the benefits, or frustrations, with run-flat tires? Regardless, the 2016 Miata has now arrived and it&#x2019;s supposed to be as good as the original from the mid-1990s. It&#x2019;s as light as the original, and yet it looks less smiley and more angry. I like that; &#x201C;passion pink&#x201D; isn&#x2019;t really my style anyway &#x2014; \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.veoh.com\u002Fwatch\u002Fv18489941r8JhBxs7?h1=Alex+%22Pink%22+Lloyd\"\u003Enot any more\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, at least. And at 155 horsepower, it&#x2019;s as slow a one-legged hound. Which means for an affordable price, you can squeal around bends like an idiot, enjoying the drive of your life, and yet you&#x2019;ll only be doing 14 mph. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"540\" height=\"360\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F9e193a304de4998491e478b591572d5502a41d3c.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fautos\u002Fresearch\u002Fvolkswagen\u002Fgolf-gti\"\u003EVolkswagen Golf GTI\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe 2015 Golf GTI was our \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fautos\u002Fbp\u002Fthe-2015-yahoo-autos-car-of-the-year--volkswagen-golf-gti-012823997.html\"\u003EYahoo Autos Car of the Year\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. It&#x2019;s brilliant, and it remains the best Golf Volkswagen has made in years &#x2014; especially if you option it with the electronic differential. The new Golf lapped our COTY autocross course faster than a \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fautos\u002Fresearch\u002Fsubaru\u002Fwrx\"\u003ESubaru WRX\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&#xA0;and&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fautos\u002Fresearch\u002Fford\u002Fmustang\u002F2016\u002F2dr-fastback-ecoboost\"\u003EFord Mustang EcoBoost\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. And on the mountainous country roads, it was a machine you could exploit the limits of at a safe, legal speed. It was engaging to drive in every environment &#x2014; from tooling around the shops to lighting up a racetrack &#x2014; which is precisely what we&#x2019;re looking for here.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"540\" height=\"360\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F88d6b38bb1ffdd04a26432e39eef152ee56ac22c.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fautos\u002Fresearch\u002Ffiat\u002F500\u002F2015\u002F2dr-hb-abarth\"\u003EFiat 500 Abarth\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EI love the Fiat 500. Built out of a joint collaboration between Subaru and Toyota, the BRZ\u002FFR-S are like the Miata &#x2014; they&#x2019;re just good, cheap, fun sports cars. The handling is well balanced, the power is minimal, and they run on low-drag tires from a \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fyahoo.com\u002Fautos\u002Fresearch\u002Ftoyota\u002Fprius\"\u003EToyota Prius\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. This means you can do giant skids at, like, 12 mph. You can be Ken Block, legally, on public roads. (Well, sort of, if you get my drift.)\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"540\" height=\"329\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002Fd85c447346c376ffbe574f296ed212f980cf846a.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fautos\u002Fresearch\u002Fford\u002Ffiesta\u002F2016\u002F5dr-hb-st\"\u003EFord Fiesta ST\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe Fiesta ST is the best compact hatchback on the market. It&#x2019;s better than the \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fautos\u002Fresearch\u002Fford\u002Ffocus\u002F2016\u002F5dr-hb-st\"\u003EFocus ST\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, and maybe even the GTI (if we&#x2019;re purely looking at the fun chart). It is, however, limited in use due to its diminutive size, but for the purpose of this question, it&#x2019;s hard to beat. Whether driving slow or fast, the Fiesta ST is a riot. And fast is never that fast. Smiles for dollar &#x2014; if your combover dictates soft tops like the Miata are generally not advised &#x2014; then the Fiesta ST is probably best of the bunch. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"540\" height=\"340\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F79f271790069f544f92450bc0c000e79f8684501.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.morgan3wheeler.co.uk\u002Fsmallsite\u002Fsmallindex5.html#intro1\"\u003EMorgan 3 Wheeler\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EOr maybe it isn&#x2019;t. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EOK, so the Morgan 3 Wheeler doesn&#x2019;t handle that great (a reason the three wheeled race car never caught on in global motorsports) and it definitely isn&#x2019;t combover-appropriate. Plus, at over $50,000, it&#x2019;s the most expensive on this list. But consider the &#x201C;fun&#x201D; aspect and it&#x2019;s hard to deny that cruising anywhere in this bizarre three wheeler wouldn&#x2019;t be awesome: The wind in your hair; the bugs in your teeth. You&#x2019;d need to wear a silly set of goggles, just because. People would stop and stare, probably assuming you&#x2019;re John Cleese gone mad. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ESometimes we forget that driving isn&#x2019;t always about practicality, or getting from A to B. It&#x2019;s not just about power and 0-60 mph speeds or useless quarter mile times. 700+ horsepower is all well and good, as is a badass name like &#x201C;Hellcat,&#x201D; but the real essence of driving is about passion &#x2014; it&#x2019;s a connection between you, the vehicle, the tarmac, and your surroundings. It should feel evocative. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAll these cars listed above excel at low speeds. They&#x2019;ll make you feel alive and in many cases perform mundane chores as well. As a race car driver, I love fast cars as much the next guy. But for my money, the cheap, usable models you see here are a more accessible form of daily enjoyment. After all, nothing beats driving a slow car fast. 1950s-era European microcar that looks equal parts cool and ridiculous. For this year's Geneva Motor Show, Toyota has taken the idea of a three-wheel, tandem-seat microcar to a modern extreme in a concept it calls [...]","type":"story","body":"\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Foy\u002Fphotos\u002Ftoyota-i-road-concept-vehicle-slideshow\u002F\"\u003E\u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Flo\u002Fapi\u002Fres\u002F1.2\u002FyAG.fSOa_JBEoKULPPI2ow--\u002FYXBwaWQ9bWFnYXppbmVzO3c9ODAw\u002Fhttps:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fos\u002Fen-US\u002Fblogs\u002Fmotoramic\u002Ftoyotairoadtop.jpg\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-10448 editorial\" alt=\"Toyota i-ROAD concept revives the three-wheel microcar\" width=\"800\" height=\"386\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EIn Terry Gilliam&apos;s classic movie &quot;Brazil,&quot; Sam Lowry drives around a dystopian future cityscape in a three-wheel Messerschmitt KR200, a 1950s-era European microcar that looks equal parts cool and ridiculous. For this year&apos;s Geneva Motor Show, \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fautos.yahoo.com\u002Ftoyota\" target=\"_blank\"\u003EToyota\u003C\u002Fa\u003E has taken the idea of a three-wheel, tandem-seat microcar to a modern extreme in a concept it calls i-ROAD, and because the future has more in common with &quot;Brazil&quot; than we might prefer.\u003Cspan id=\"more-10447\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EMost major automakers are working on ideas of vehicles that fill the space between a small car and a motorcycle &#x2014; something small enough to fit in tight urban environments, but sizable enough to provide weather and crash protection so that passengers wouldn&apos;t have to wear helmets. None has advanced to the point of production, and the slow progress of a few start-ups has made such vehicles seem an answer to a question not many people have thought to ask yet.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EBut the trend lines say rising fuel prices and crowded metropolises will eventually demand a replacement for the four-wheel compact car. In the i-ROAD, Toyota combines an electric motor and battery that can travel 30 miles on a charge with a stability system to keep the trike upright; its front wheels raise and lower in turns to lean the body without toppling it. By seating two people in tandem, Toyota says the i-ROAD is no wider than a conventional motorcycle, and would require no special training to drive.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Foy\u002Fphotos\u002Ftoyota-i-road-concept-vehicle-slideshow\u002F\"\u003E\u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-10450 editorial\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"407\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Flo\u002Fapi\u002Fres\u002F1.2\u002F3JAtHV7crzVzqxHJ3CCBxw--\u002FYXBwaWQ9bWFnYXppbmVzO3c9ODAw\u002Fhttps:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fos\u002Fen-US\u002Fblogs\u002Fmotoramic\u002Ftoyotairoadcombo-copy.jpg\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThe chances of Toyota building a 21st-century Messerschmitt hover close to zero at the moment; the world&apos;s largest automaker has plenty of demand for its real vehicles, and as the \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Foy\u002Fscion\u002FiQ\" target=\"_blank\"\u003EScion iQ\u003C\u002Fa\u003E shows, four-wheel cars can get far smaller than most people find comfortable.
